#BlackHistoryMonth 	Harriet Tubman escaped slavery to become a leading abolitionist. She led hundreds of enslaved people to freedom along the route of the Underground Railroad. https://t.co/IrIG4Z6XPa
#BlackHistoryMonth Famed 19th-century author and orator Frederick Douglass was an eminent human rights leader in the anti-slavery movement and the first African-American citizen to hold a high U.S. government rank. https://t.co/hPCjCQls6t
Another outstanding man during the Mexican Independence, #JoseMariaMorelos was the son of #afromexicans  Together with Vicente Guerrero, abolished slavery in October 1813. #BlackHistoryMonth https://t.co/30JtcRflGf
Not many people know this, but #VicenteGuerrero who was one of the leading generals of the Mexican War of Independence, and later served as President of Mexico, was of Afro-Mestizo descent. He abolished slavery during his brief term as president. #BlackHistoryMonth #afromexicans https://t.co/XaLuEg2vv2
#Mexico has 1.4 million #AfricanMexicans mostly located in Guerrero, Oaxaca, Veracruz, Mexico City and small settlements in northern Mexico. Many of their ancestors came from Spain as slaves, others came running away from the US during the #MexicanRevolution #BlackHistoyMonth https://t.co/Y7QreItbod
#BlackHistoryMonth began as a way for remembering important people and events in the history of the #AfricanDiaspora. It is celebrated annually in the United States in February since 1970, thanks to black educators and the Black United Students at Kent State University. https://t.co/t0O0u098Eu
